                 Town Board Regular Meeting Minutes 
                      Tuesday, January 7, 2025 – 2:00 PM 
                                        
      

I.    Call to Order 

      The meeting was called to order at 2:04 PM by Supervisor Tim Hubbard 
       
  Attendee Name                     Title            Status       Arrived 
  Tim Hubbard               Supervisor             Present       
  Kenneth Rothwell          Councilman             Present       
  Robert Kern               Councilman             Present       
  Denise Merrifield         Councilwoman           Present       
  Joann Waski               Councilwoman           Present       

II.   Notice 

      1. 1-7-25 Notice of TB Meeting with 1 Public Hearing  
       

III.  Invocation-Pastor Dupree- Living Water Full Gospel Church 

IV.   Announcements 

V.    Correspondence 

      1. Letter from Board of Directors Riverhead BIDMA - Town Square 
         Development  
       

VI.   Reports 

VII.  Public Hearings 

   Public Hearing Opened at 2:13 PM by Supervisor Hubbard. Greg Bergman from 
   planning presented an overview of project, Brian Stark the Applicant explained the 
   needs and uses associated with expansion. Kim Judd, Esq clarified the SEQRA 
   process and timelines in regards to abandoned buildings. Public Comments via 
   Zoom-Kathy McGraw praised reuse and project but questioned the SEQRA process 
   and timeline for reestablishing a non conforming use. John Weiss a neighbor to 
   project showed support and appreciated the improvements.   


For more information visit our website at www.townofriverheadny.gov  
                                         

        - 2:00 PM Public Hearing-Special Permit Sandy Pond Golf Course  
       

VIII. Comments on Resolutions 

   Kathy McGraw via Zoom, Resolution 88. Voiced opposition to settlement with Island 
   Water Park. 
   John Kellerher- Voiced opposition to settlement with Island Water Park. 
   Mike Foley via Zoom- Resolution 9, supported general salary increases for 
   employees; questioned future actions of Island Water Park after settlement. 
   Mark Conrad- Resolution 83 and concerns of bio-solids and future plans to dispose 
   of same. 
   Barbara Blass-Resolution 88, concerning DEC permits and violations of site plan in 
   regards to allowed expansions.

PLEASE TAKE NOTICE that the Town Board Meeting scheduled for January 7, 2025 at 2:00 p.m.

      which is as follows: townofriverheadny.viebit.com/player_live.php

is as follows:

           existing non-conforming commercial use which currently consists of a 9-
           hole executive golf course, an 18-hole mini golf course, with the

01.07.2025                                                    ADOPTED 
 
 
                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-1 
                                        
      ESTABLISHES CAPITAL PROJECT #12426 MEETINGHOUSE CREEK 
                               RESTORATION 
                                        
               Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
                    which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
      WHEREAS, Meetinghouse Creek, located in the Town of Riverhead, is listed as 
an impaired waterbody (i.e. NYSDEC Priority Waterbodies Lists) due to low dissolved 
oxygen concentrations caused by excessive nutrient levels from agricultural runoff, 
stormwater/urban runoff, municipal discharges, and boat pollution; and 
       
      WHEREAS, the upstream limit of the surface waters of Meetinghouse Creek is 
located on a 2.61-acre parcel owned by the Town of Riverhead, located at 705 Main 
Road, Aquebogue, NY, more particularly described as SCTM No. 600-67-2-27.1; and 
       
      WHEREAS, stormwater from Church Lane and NY State Route 25 (Main Road) 
discharges to the north end of the site through a 3-inch reinforced concrete pipe; and 
       
      WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead, would like to establish a Stormwater 
Wetland and Habitat Restoration project to improve water quality by managing runoff 
from Main Road and Church Lane, using a design that conforms to the New York State 
Stormwater Management Design Manual standards to accommodate Water Quality 
Volume (WQv), and Extreme Flood Control (100-year-event) to efficiently remove 
sediments and pollutants; and 
       
      WHEREAS, funding sources for this project include: the New York State’s 
Environmental Facilities Corporation Green Innovation Grant Program (NYS EFC GIGP) 
for a grant in the amount of $350,000; The Research Foundation for The State 
University of New York (SUNY RF) for a grant in the amount of $600,000; the New York 
State Department of Transportation (NYS DOT) for a grant in the amount of $50,000; 
and the Suffolk County Water Quality Protection and Restoration Program (WQPRP) for 
a grant in the amount of $235,000, for a total grant funding of $1,235,000 to be utilized 
for the Meetinghouse Creek Restoration Project.  
 
      NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Supervisor be, and is hereby 
authorized to establish the following budget adjustments; 
       
                                                FROM              TO 
 
H01-3789-000-12426-H State Aid – EFC           $350,000 
H01-3789-100-12426-H State Aid – SUNY RF       $600,000 
H01-3789-200-12426-H State Aid – NYS DOT        $ 50,000 
H01-2706-000-12426-7  County Aid – WQPRP      $235,000 
 

                                                                          Packet Pg. 22                                                                                 9.1
H01-1-1940-230-000-12426 – Improvements                           $1,235,000 
 
 
And be it further 
 
      RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a copy of this 
resolution to Finance@townofriverheadny.gov, the Community Development and 
Engineering Departments, and be it further  
       
      RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
      SECONDER:    Robert Kern, Councilman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-2 
                                        
   ESTABLISHES CAPITAL PROJECT #12425 FOR TOWN OWNED ALLEYWAY 
                              ENHANCEMENTS 
                                        
                 Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
                 which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
      WHEREAS, Town Board Resolution 2022-397 supports, endorses, and 
authorizes pursuit of Suffolk County Downtown Revitalization Round 20 funding for 
enhancements to a Town owned alleyway located south of the Suffolk Theater. The 
enhancements include installing motion activated lighting that will be designed by an 
artist specializing in “light art” to enhance safety, walkability and access to Main Street 
for pedestrians using the alleyway. Pursuant to this resolution, the Town intends to 
officially establish a capital project for the enhancements. And, 
 
      WHEREAS, funding for this project will be made available through the following 
sources: $16,737.50 from Round 20 of the Suffolk County Downtown Revitalization 
Grant Program, $13,262.50 of grant funding from the Riverhead Business Improvement 
District, and $10,000 to come from the Town of Riverhead’s CDBG funds, for a 
combined total of $40,000.  
 
      NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Supervisor be, and is hereby 
authorized to establish the following budget adjustments; 
       
                                                FROM              TO 
 
H01-1-1940-230-000-12425      Improvements      $16,000.00 
H01-1-1940-435-000-12425  
              Professional Services – Engineering $24,000.00 
       
      H01-2706-000-12425-7    County Aid                          $16,737.50 
      H01-2705-000-12425-7    BIDMA Grant                         $13,262.50 
      H01-4097-000-12425-H    Federal Aid                         $10,000.00 
 
 
And be it further 
 
      RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a copy of this 
resolution to Finance@townofriverheadny.gov, and the Community Development 
Department, and be it further  
       
      RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.

York,  11901);  and  one  (1)  unimproved  lot  located  at  SCTM#  0600-065.00-01.00-
019.000  (aka,  18  Oak  Drive,  Riverhead,  New  York,  11901)  with  the  expressed  intent 
that these parcels be transferred to Habitat for Humanity of Suffolk for development as 
workforce  housing  at  no  cost  to  the  Town  of  Riverhead  through  a  partnership  with 
Habitat for Humanity of Suffolk; and 
       
      WHEREAS,  the  above  parcels  were  subsequently  transferred  by  the  Town  of 
Riverhead to Habitat for Humanity through the 72-H program for affordable housing via 
Quitclaim Deed for no consideration; and  
       
      WHEREAS, Habitat for Humanity has since requested building permits from the 
Town of Riverhead Building Department for the construction of single-family residences 
located at the above parcels; and 
 
      WHEREAS,  the  Town  of  Riverhead  and  the  Town  of  Riverhead  Community 
Development  Agency  (CDA)  Board  desires  to  foster  the  continued  development  of 
workforce housing infrastructure to retain critically important members of our community  
that  typically qualify  for  qualify  for  workforce  housing  including  to  the  extent  possible, 
Veterans of the United States Armed Forces, young professionals, nurses and nurses 
aids,  teachers,  entry-level  public  safety  personnel,  grocery  clerks,  secretaries, 
mechanics,  accounting  clerks,  retail  and  restaurant  employees,  and  many  other  jobs 
integral to a balanced community; and 
 
      NOW,  THEREFORE  BE  IT  RESOLVED,  that  in  consideration  of  the  unique 
circumstances above,  the Town Board does hereby authorize the Building Department 
to waive the fees for the Building Permits issued to Habitat for Humanity in connection 
with  the  construction  of  single  family  residences  upon  the  parcels  known  and 
designated  as  SCTM#  0600-126.000-04.00-039.000  (aka,  508  St.  John’s  Place, 
Riverhead,  New  York,  11901);  and  SCTM#  0600-065.00-01.00-019.000  (aka,  18  Oak 
Drive, Riverhead, New York, 11901), nunc pro tunc; and be it further,  
 
      RESOLVED,   that  the  Resolution  is  adopted  pursuant  to  MHR§10(i)(ii)(a)(12); 
and be it further, 
 

                                                                          Packet Pg. 30                                                                                 9.4
      RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a copy of this 
resolution  to  Habitat  for  Humanity  of  Long  Island Jimmy@habitatliny.org,  the  Building 
Department and the Office of the Town Attorney, and be it further  
 
      RESOLVED,  that  all  Town  Hall  Departments  may  review and  obtain  a  copy  of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a copy of same may be 
obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
      SECONDER:    Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

01.07.2025                                                    ADOPTED 
 
 
                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-5 
                                        
     RATIFIES AUTHORIZATION FOR EMPLOYEE TO BUY-BACK ACCRUED 
                               VACATION TIME 
                                        
               Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
                    which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
      WHEREAS,  David  Zebrowski,  is a  Building  Maintenance  Manager  overseeing 
the  Buildings  and  Grounds  Division  of  the  Riverhead  Town  Engineering  Department; 
and  
       
      WHEREAS,  due  to  limited  availability  of  supervisory  level  staffing  within  the 
Buildings  &  Grounds  Division  and  exacerbated  by  increased  work  load  due  to 
maintenance  of  mechanicals,  roof  repairs,  etc.  at  Town  Hall,  rehabilitation  of  Town 
Annex to ready for occupancy, and a plethora of other non-scheduled yet time sensitive 
projects, the Engineering Department (and at times, Town, for urgent or time sensitive 
projects) did not approve and Mr. Zebrowski was unable to schedule and utilize accrued 
time during the 2024 calendar year; and 
       
      NOW,  THEREFORE  BE  IT  RESOLVED,  that  in  recognition  of  Mr.  Zebrowski’s 
dedication and tireless work for the Town during 2024 and at times sole supervision of 
projects, repairs etc. without benefit of other managerial or supervisory staff within the 
Buildings  &  Grounds  Division  to  assist  or  assume  the  necessary  managerial  or 
supervisory role, the Town Board be and hereby ratifies effective September 1st 2024 
the  authorization  for  Mr.  Zebrowski  to  buy-back  and  the  Office  of  the  Financial 
Administrator to process payment for the expiring of 78.25 accrued vacation hours, and 
be it further,    
       
      RESOLVED, that the Town Engineers shall be responsible, including assuming 
the role of supervisor on some projects, to better address work load and assignments of 
staff  such  that  employees  such  as  Mr.  Zebrowski  can  utilize  vacation  time  and  the 
Engineering Department and staff within the Engineering Department are requested to 
advise employees  within  their  supervision of  deadlines  for  buy  back  and  notices  from 
payroll to avoid detriment to employees for failure to timely buyback; and 
       
       RESOLVED, Mr. Zebrowski shall not be permitted late requests for buyback in 
the  future  and  instead  as  stated  in  the  “Resolved”  above,  Mr.  Zebrowski,  must 
communicate his desire to the Town Engineers and schedule for vacation such that his 
requests may reasonably be accommodated; and 
       
      RESOLVED Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward a copy of this resolution to 
Personnel Director, the Town Attorney’s Office and the Financial Administrator; and  
 


                                                                          Packet Pg. 33                                                                                 9.5
      RESOLVED,  that  all  Town  Hall  Departments  may  review and  obtain  a  copy  of 
this  resolution  from  the  electronic  storage  device  and,  if  needed,  a  certified  copy  of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.   
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
      SECONDER:    Robert Kern, Councilman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-7 
                                        
 AUTHORIZATION TO PUBLISH A HELP WANTED ADVERTISEMENT FOR PART-
                           TIME POLICE OFFICERS 
                                        
             Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
                  which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
            RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is authorized to publish and post the 
      below  advertisement as a help wanted advertisement in the January 9, 2025, 
      issue of the News Review.  
 
 
                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                           POSITIONS AVAILABLE  
             
            PLEASE TAKE NOTICE, the Town of Riverhead is seeking candidates for 
      the  purpose  of  serving  as  Part-time  Police  Officers  with  the  Riverhead  Police 
      Department. Candidates must be a U.S. Citizen and have reached 20 years of 
      age at the time of application, be a high school graduate, possess a valid NYS 
      Driver’s license, possess a Municipal Police Training Certificate OR attend and 
      complete  the  Suffolk  County  Police  Academy  training  course TENTATIVELY 
      scheduled  to  commence  in  the  Fall  of  2025.  Additionally,  candidates  must 
      successfully pass a psychological evaluation, medical evaluation, physical fitness 
      agility  evaluation  and  polygraph  exam.  Applications  are  available  at  Police 
      Headquarters, 210 Howell Avenue, Riverhead NY 11901 and must be submitted 
      to  the  Office  of  the  Chief  of  Police  no  later  than  March  28,  2025.  For  further 
      information, call Riverhead Police Department at (631) 727-4500, ext. 315. 
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
      SECONDER:    Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

             Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
                  which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
      WHEREAS, due to the resignation of the incumbent, there is a vacancy for Water 
Treatment Plant Operator Trainee in the Water District of the Town of Riverhead; 
 
      WHEREAS, the Suffolk County Department of Civil Service has certified a list for 
the title of Water Treatment Plant Operator Trainee, List #24AF660, the list was duly 
canvased in accordance with civil service regulations, interviews were conducted, and 
as a result, a recommendation of a suitable candidate has been made by the Personnel 
Committee. 
 
      NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that pending the results of a 
successfully completed background investigation, this Town Board hereby appoints 
Christopher Calderon to the position of Water Treatment Plant Operator Trainee 
effective January 13, 2025 and sets his salary at a rate of pay as found on Group 9, 
Step P of the CSEA Operational and Technical Salary Schedule which is $ 56,111.91 
per annum. 
 
      RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.

                      APPOINTS A BUDGET ASSISTANT 
                                        
               Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
                  which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
      WHEREAS, Brittney Miller has been serving as a provisional appointment in the 
position of Budget Assistant since October 17, 2023; and 
 
      WHEREAS, on December 27, 2024 the Suffolk County Department of Civil 
Service established a certified List of Eligibles, list # 24AF811, for the position of Budget 
Assistant, and Brittney Miller is immediately reachable on the County List; and 
 
      WHEREAS, Civil Service regulations require that a permanent appointment of a 
provisional employee be made within sixty days of the date a Certified List of Eligibles is 
first established.  
 
      NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that pursuant to Civil Service 
regulations, this Town Board hereby removes the provisional status of Brittney Miller 
and appoints her to the title of Budget Assistant effective today, January 7, 2025 at no 
change to her current salary or other level of benefits. 
 
      RESOLVED, that Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this 
resolution from the electronic storage device, and if needed, a certified copy of same 
can be obtained from the office of the Town Clerk.

                                                                                                          Packet Pg. 93                                                                                9.21.a
       
                                APPENDIX B 
                                        
                            FEES AND EXPENSES 
       
       
      The fees for our services for capital project financings will not exceed the following: Serial 
Bonds - $8,500 for each bond issue with an Official Statement and $0.60 per $1,000 thereafter, 
prior to the reduction of premium; Refunding Serial Bonds - $12,500 for each bond issue with an 
Official Statement plus $1.75 per $1,000 thereafter, based on total proceeds; Bond Anticipation 
Notes – Base fee of $5,500 for each note and $0.50 per $1,000 thereafter; Lease financings - $7,500; 
Environmental Facilities Corporation Financings plus $0.75 per $1,000 over $3,000,000.  The fee 
for general consulting services will be $150 per hour with the terms of the service agreed upon prior 
to the engagement. 
       
      The fee for preparation and filing of the Statement of Annual Financial and Operating 
Information in accordance with SEC Rule 15c2-12, and the Town’s Continuing Disclosure 
Undertaking will be $2,500.  There is no charge for the filing of material event notices. 
       
      All of the above fees represent our experience in working with local governments for the 
last several years, a general understanding of the capital project plans and the necessary time 
expected to execute each transaction.  It should be noted that these fees represent a “not to exceed” 
amount.  Munistat has historically discounted much of the above fees due to size, the issuance of 
more than one bond issue in a given year, or single-purpose borrowings. 
       
      The fee for our services includes all out-of-pocket expenses. Other normal issuing costs, 
such as bond counsel fees, rating agency fees and publication of resolutions and Notices of Sale are 
billed directly to the Town by the respective parties.  
 
      Munistat Services, Inc. will not charge to attend meetings of the Board, work sessions, 
meetings with bond counsel, ratings agencies, or any other meetings associated with a capital 
project.  We do not charge any fees for services delivered prior to a referendum, including 
preparation of estimated debt service and tax rate impact schedules.  There will be no charge until, 
and unless the closing of the bonds or notes take place. 
 
                                                                                      Attachment:  Munistat -Financial Advisor Fee Schedule 2025 (2025-21 : Appoints Financial Advisor)

                                                                                                          Packet Pg. 96                                                                                9.22.a
 

Proposed Fee Schedule - 2025 

                                    Bonds 

      Our fee relating to a publicly sold serial bond issue would include a base charge of $2,500 
for the preparation of proceedings relating to the sale and issuance of the bonds.  In addition, we 
would charge a bond issuance fee of: 

      $0.85 per $1,000 for the first $5,000,000 financed 
       
      $.60 per $1,000 for the next $5,000,000 financed 
       
      $.40 per $1,000 thereafter. 

      The above calculation would be limited to a maximum of $9,000. 

                                       Notes 

      Our fee for publicly sold note issues, including bond anticipation notes, tax anticipation 
notes,  revenue  anticipation  notes,  capital  notes,  budget  notes  and  deficiency  notes,  whether 
original or renewal issues, or issues which combine new obligations with renewal obligations, 
would include a base charge of $500, plus a fee of: 

      $ .50 per $1,000 for the first $3,000,000 financed 

      $ .40 per $1,000 for the next $3,000,000 financed 

      $ .30 per $1,000 thereafter. 

      The above calculation would be limited to a maximum of $4,000. 

                       Bonds Sold by Private Sale or Negotiated Sale 

      For statutory installment bonds or bonds sold by private sale or negotiated sale, the base 
charge would be reduced to $1,000 and the maximum fee would be $4,500.  

                            Bond Resolution Preparation Fees 

      Our fee for the preparation of bond resolutions would be $200 per bond resolution.  Such 
fee would generally be billed together with our fees for the initial serial bonds or bond anticipation 
notes issued pursuant to such bond resolution(s).  
                                                                                      Attachment:  Hawkins Delafield and Wood - Bond Counsel Fee Schedule 2025 (2025-22 : Appoints Counsel)


 
                                                               3952217.1  047550  AGMT 
                                                                          Packet Pg. 97                                                                                9.22.a
 

                                  Disclosure Review 

      In the event  that an Official Statement is  prepared and circulated in  connection with  a 
particular issuance of bonds or notes, we would request to be compensated in the amount of $750 
for any time spent reviewing such disclosure document.  This fee would include preparation of the 
Continuing Disclosure or Material Events Undertaking and any related advice and. 

                 Refunding Bonds and Issues Sold by Negotiated Sale 

      Due to many variables involved with refunding bond issues (whether sold by competitive 
or negotiated sale) and other bond and note issues which may be sold by negotiated sale (e.g., 
issues not subject to public sale requirements), we would propose that the fees for such issues be 
mutually  agreed  upon  on  a  per-transaction  basis,  based  on  the  nature  and  complexity  of  the 
financing, prior to commencing work on any such particular transaction. 

                              District Proceedings 

      In relation to the preparation of proceedings pursuant to Town Law §202-b for the increase 
and improvement of facilities of an existing Town district, or pursuant to Town Law §209-h for 
increasing the maximum amount to be expended for a Town district project, our fee would be 
$1,750.  For the establishment of a new Town district or improvement area pursuant to Town Law 
Articles 12, 12-A or 12-C, our fee for preparing the necessary proceedings would be $2,000.   

                                     Hourly Fees 

      In the normal course, we would not expect to bill the Town for any additional hourly time.  
However, the scope of bond counsel services required in connection with a particular financing 
sometimes requires additional services.  In such event, we would propose to charge a fee of $200 
per hour for attorney time spent on unusual matters, other than those expected to be encountered 
in the usual course of a bond or note issue.  If circumstances dictate that a different rate (lower or 
higher) be used, we would discuss an alternate rate with the Town prior to commencing work. 

      If the Town should request specialized federal securities law or tax law services, including 
services relating to the preparation of arbitrage rebate reports or related work, or services relating 
to IRS or SEC audits or inquiries, we would propose charging for our services in accordance with 
our usual fee schedule for these specific services but we would discuss the specific fees with the 
Town prior to the commencement of any work. 

                                 Incidental Expenses 

      We would not bill the Town for any out-of-pocket expenses or disbursements. 
 
                                                                                      Attachment:  Hawkins Delafield and Wood - Bond Counsel Fee Schedule 2025 (2025-22 : Appoints Counsel)


 
                                                               3952217.1  047550  AGMT

     RENEWS THE APPOINTMENT OF LEGAL REPRESENTATION FOR THE 
                             PLANNING BOARD 
                                        
             Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
                  which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
      WHEREAS, Erik Howard Esq., Town Attorney, and Danielle Hurley, who 
presently serves as Deputy Town Attorney, expressed a willingness and desire to share 
the additional duties as co-special counsel to the Planning Board; and

them as such beginning January 1, 2024; and 
       
      NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, the Town Board renews the 
appointment Erik Howard, Esq., Town Attorney, and Danielle Hurley, Esq., to serve as 
co-special counsel for the Planning Board effective January 1, 2025 and assigns 
additional duties shared equally, including but not limited to, general representation to 
the Planning Board, appearance at Planning Board meetings, work sessions, and 
drafting opinions at an annual rate of pay of $12,000.00, with each receiving $6000.00 
annually to be paid on biweekly basis with no other change to the terms and conditions 
of employment; and

Office of Accounting and the Planning Board; and be it further,

                            TB Resolution 2025-24 
                                        
             RE-APPOINTS A ZONING OFFICER, NUNC PRO TUNC 
                                        
               Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
                  which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
      WHEREAS,    resolution  #2023-525 and  thereafter  resolution  2024-117  were 
adopted by the Riverhead Town Board designating Greg Bergman as a Zoning Officer 
to the Department of Land Management, effective July 3, 2023 until December 31, 2023 
and then January 1, 2024 through December 31, 2024 respectively; and  
                      
      WHEREAS,  there  is  a  continued  need  for  a  Zoning  Officer  to  assist  in  the 
Planning Department with review, processing and approval of permits and applications 
and  rendering  zoning  determinations  in  connection  with  applications  and  plans 
submitted to the Department of Land Management pursuant to the rules and regulations 
of the Town of Riverhead. 
                                        
      NOW,  THEREFORE,  BE  IT  RESOLVED,  that  the  Town  Board  hereby  re-
appoints Greg Bergman as  Zoning  Officer, Nunc  Pro  Tunc,  effective  January 1, 2025 
through December 31, 2025, unless terminated earlier by Town Board Resolution; and 
be it further, 
 
      RESOLVED,  as  Zoning  Officer,  Bergman  shall  have  the  authority  to  review, 
process  and  approve  permits  and  applications  and  render  zoning  determinations  in 
connection  with  applications  and  plans  submitted  to  the  Department  of  Land 
Management  pursuant  to  the  zoning  codes,  rules,  and  regulations  of  the  Town  of 
Riverhead; and be it further, 
 
      RESOLVED, Bergman shall be entitled to a stipend in the sum of $3,000.00 per 
year  made  in equal,  biweekly  payments  in  connection  with  the  additional  duties  and 
designation set forth herein effective January 1, 2025; and be it further,  
 
      RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby directed to forward a copy of 
this resolution to Greg Bergman, Office of Personnel, the Office of the Town Attorney 
and the Office of Land Management; and be it further  
 
      RESOLVED,   all  Town  Hall  Departments  may  review  and  obtain  a  copy  of  this 
resolution  from  the  electronic  storage  device  and  if  needed,  a  certified copy  of  same

                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-29 
                                        
 RATIFIES THE RECLASSIFICATION OF A HEAVY EQUIPMENT OPERATOR TO 
                  CONSTRUCTION EQUIPMENT OPERATOR 
                                        
               Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
                    which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
      WHEREAS,   the  Suffolk  County  Department  of  Civil  Service  has  reviewed  the 
duties  of  Heavy  Equipment  Operator  Robert  Tedesco,  and  has  subsequently 
reclassified his position to that of a Construction Equipment Operator; and 
       
      WHEREAS, Robert Tedesco’s qualifications makes him appointable to the title of 
Construction  Equipment  Operator,  and  his department  head  and  the  Town  Board  are 
willing to appoint him to same.  
       
      RESOLVED, that this Town Board hereby approves the reclassification of Robert 
Tedesco’s  position  and appoints  him  to  the  title  of  Construction  Equipment  Operator 
effective  January  1,  2025,  placing  his  salary  at  Group  9  Step  12A  of  the  CSEA 
Operational and Technical Salary Schedule which is $70,198.04 per annum; and 
 
      RESOLVED,   that  all Town  Hall  Departments  may  review  and  obtain  a  copy  of 
this  resolution  from  the  electronic  storage  device,  and  if  needed,  a  certified  copy  of 
same can be obtained from the office of the Town Clerk.   
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
      SECONDER:    Robert Kern, Councilman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

                                                                                                          Packet Pg. 126                                                                                 9.36
 
01.07.2025                                                    ADOPTED 
 
 
                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-36 
                                        
     APPROVES SALARY ADJUSTMENT FOR A LEGISLATIVE SECRETARY 
                                        
               Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
                  which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
      WHEREAS, the US Department of Labor published a final rule to the Fair Labor 
Standards Act (FLSA) on April 26, 2024 which increases the minimum salary amount to 
be  exempt  in  the  FLSA’s  minimum  wage  and  overtime  requirements  under  section 
13(a)(1) to be $1,128 per week, which is equivalent to a $58,656.00 annual salary; and 
 
      WHEREAS,  the  Personnel  Officer  did  advise  the  Town  Board  that  one 
employee’s  exemption  status  would  be  impacted  by  this  ruling,  that  employee  being 
Diane Tucci, Legislative Secretary; and 
 
      NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, in the effort to maintain her exemption 
status as it was upon hire on January 8, 2024 the Town Board hereby approves a salary 
increase for Diane Tucci effective January 1, 2025 to be $58,656.00 as set forth in the 
resolution setting salaries for 2025 with no other change to her terms or conditions of 
employment; and  
 
      BE IT FURTHER, RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk provide a copy of this 
resolution to the Accounting Department and Legislative Secretary Diane Tucci, 
 
      BE  IT  FURTHER,  RESOLVED,  all  Town  Hall  Departments  may  review  and 
obtain  a  copy  of  this  resolution  from  the  electronic  storage  device  and  if  needed,  a 
certified copy of same from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
      SECONDER:    Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-37 
                                        
   APPROVES SALARY ADJUSTMENTS FOR PUBLIC SAFETY DISPATCHERS 
                                        
               Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
                    which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
      WHEREAS, the Chief of Police, Edward Frost, has requested a salary increase 
for the personnel of public safety dispatchers: Kim Baird, Deborah Buyukdeniz, Erin 
Chester, Jasmine Dyson, Jessica Eibs-Stankaitis, Melissa Elco, William Fleming, 
Patrick Gabriele, Patricia Lopez, Tanya Newman and Tara Sinclair; and 
 
      WHEREAS, the Town Board did meet with Chief Frost to review and discuss the 
request for the salary increases; and 
       
      NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, the Town Board recognizes the need for 
a competitive salary as the minimum wage continues to increase, the Town Board 
hereby approves an increase in annual salary effective January 1, 2025 with no other 
change to the terms or conditions of employment. The current and new salaries are 
found on the CSEA Public Safety Dispatcher (PSD) salary schedule and are outlined 
below. 


                                                                               
       
      BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain  
a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified  
copy of same from the Office of the Town Clerk.

                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-38 
                                        
      APPROVES SALARY ADJUSTMENTS FOR NAMED WATER DISTRICT 
                                EMPLOYEES 
                                        
                 Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
                 which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
      WHEREAS, the Water District Superintendent, Frank Mancini, has requested a 
salary increase specified Water District personnel: Kyle Kochanskyj, Keith Albee and 
Travis Rocco; and 
 
      WHEREAS, the Town Board did meet with the Water District Superintendent, 
Frank Mancini to review and discuss the request for the salary increases; and 
       
      NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, the Town Board recognizes the need for 
a competitive salary in the Water district in order to compete with larger water supplier 
organizations, the Town Board hereby approves an increase in annual salary effective 
January 1, 2025 with no other change to the terms or conditions of employment. The 
current and new salaries are found on the Operational & Technical salary schedule and 
are outlined below. 
       
      Kyle Kochanskyj, Maintenance Mechanic II move to group 7, step 6 at a salaried 
rate of $58,430.49 
      Keith Albee, Water Treatment Plant Operator IIB move to group 15, step 5 at a 
salaried rate of $65,220.27 
      Travis Rocco, Water Treatment Plant Operator IIB move to group 15, step 5 at a 
salaried rate of $65,220.27 
       
      BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain  
a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified  
copy of same from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Robert Kern, Councilman 
      SECONDER:    Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-54 
                                        
      APPROVES SALARY INCREASE FOR CHIEF BUILDING INSPECTOR 
                                        
                 Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
                 which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
      WHEREAS, Community Development Project Supervisor, Dawn Thomas has 
requested a salary increase for Chief Building Inspector, Andreas Sofoklis; and 
 
      WHEREAS, the Town Board did meet with Community Development Project 
Supervisor, Dawn Thomas to review and discuss her request for the salary increase; 
and 
 
      NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, in recognition of Chief Building Inspector 
Andreas Sofoklis’s dedication and hard work, the Town Board hereby approves an 
increase in annual salary effective January 1, 2025 in addition to the salary set forth in 
resolution setting salaries for 2025 with no other change to his terms or conditions of 
employment to grade 9 step 16A on the CSEA Administrative salary schedule of 
$122,870.24; and  
 
      BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk provide a copy of this 
resolution to the Accounting Department, Community Development Project Supervisor 
Dawn Thomas, and Chief Building Inspector Andreas Sofoklis; and, 
 
      BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain  
a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified  
copy of same from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Robert Kern, Councilman 
      SECONDER:    Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

                                                                                                          Packet Pg. 192                                                                                 9.69
 
01.07.2025                                                    ADOPTED 
 
 
                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-69 
                                        
  APPROVES A STIPEND FOR A SPANISH SPEAKING JUSTICE COURT CLERK 
                                        
               Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
                    which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
      WHEREAS,    the  Town  Board  recognizes the  need for  a  Spanish/English 
speaking  translator to be  readily  available  for  Court  appearances  and  trials  in  the 
Riverhead Town Justice Court to readily service the Spanish speaking population of the 
Riverhead community; and 
                      
      WHEREAS,   the  Town  does  currently  contract  with  a  few  select  individuals  for 
Spanish/English  translation  services.  However,  due  to  scheduling  conflicts  or  short 
notice,  there  have  been  instances  in  which  the  Town  of  Riverhead  Justice  Court  has 
been  unable  to  obtain  translation  services  and  has  therefore  had  to  request  the 
assistance of a current Spanish Speaking Justice Court Clerk, Yenci Avelar-Gonzalez, a 
clerical  employee  who’s  position  requires  public  interaction  on  behalf  of  the  Court  in 
other capacities to provide assistance in the court room; and  
 
      WHEREAS,    a  recommendation  has  been  made  by the  Town  Justices  the 
Honorable  Sean  Walter  and  the  Honorable  Lori  Hulse to designate Yenci  Avelar-
Gonzalez, a current Spanish Speaking Justice Court Clerk, to act as a Spanish/English 
speaking  translator  within  the  Justice  Court  for  the  purpose  of  Court  proceedings 
including trials should the contracted individuals be unavailable and be compensated to 
do so. 
                                        
      NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, the Town Board hereby recognizes the 
additional  duties  being  requested  of  Yenci  Avelar-Gonzalez providing  translation 
services within the Justice Court and its proceedings; and  
 
      BE  IT  FURTHER  RESOLVED,    Yenci  Avelar-Gonzalez shall  be  entitled  to  a 
stipend  in  the  sum of $3,000.00  per year in connection  with  the additional duties  and 
designation set forth herein, effective January 1, 2025; and be it further,  
             
      RESOLVED,   all  Town  Hall  Departments  may  review  and  obtain  a  copy  of  this 
resolution  from  the  electronic  storage  device  and  if  needed,  a  certified copy  of  same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
      SECONDER:    Robert Kern, Councilman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-70 
                                        
   APPROVES THE CONTINUATION OF A STIPEND FOR TWO IT EMPLOYEES 
                                        
                 Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
                 which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
      WHEREAS, the Town had purchased a Hybrid VOIP (Voice-Over Internet 
Protocol) Telephone system to replace its landlines in January of 2020; and 
 
      WHEREAS, a stipulation was created and agreed to between the CSEA and the 
Town Supervisor at the time of the same; and 
       
      WHEREAS, the stipulation states “That two Town Employees within the 
Information Technology Division of the Finance Department shall be required to perform 
daily, weekly, and monthly maintenance of the Town’s VOIP (Voice-Over Internet 
Protocol) system, including performing system crash recovery.” and the resolution to 
accompany it, 2020-42, specifically names two employees, but only one is still 
employed, Theresa Sweeney (DeFilippis); and  
       
      WHEREAS, resolution 2024-89 was passed naming John West II as the second 
employee within the IT department to perform the duties described above. 
 
      NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board hereby approves 
the continuation of this stipend for Theresa DeFilippis and John West II for which they 
shall each receive a stipend in the sum of $3,000, annually, to be paid biweekly in equal 
amounts, commencing January 1, 2025; and  
 
      RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk provide a copy of this resolution to Network 
and Systems Specialist II Theresa (Terri) DeFilippis, Network and Systems 
Administrator Henry Kreymborg, and Network and Systems Specialist II John West; 
and,   
 
      BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain  
a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified  
copy of same from the Office of the Town Clerk.  
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Robert Kern, Councilman 
      SECONDER:    Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

01.07.2025                                                    ADOPTED 
 
 
                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-73 
                                        
AUTHORIZES THE COMMUNITY DEVELOPMENT DEPARTMENT TO APPLY FOR 
                     THE NYS ADU PLUS ONE PROGRAM 
                                        
               Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
                    which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
      WHEREAS, The Town of Riverhead has been working to provide its residents 
with relief from the home affordability crisis by creating opportunities for a variety of 
housing options including rentals and homeownership, and  
 
 
      WHEREAS, the State of NY Department of Homes and Community Renewal 
sponsors the ADU Plus One program that provides existing homeowners with the 
funding to create or legalize existing ADU’s (Accessory Dwelling Units) by providing 
income qualifying homeowners in the Town with up to $125,000.00 to create or legalize 
an ADU, and   
 
 
      WHEREAS, this program would provide relief to Riverhead homeowners who 
would like to create an ADU for a family member or long-term renter to offset housing 
expenses, and  
       
      WHEREAS, ADUs are required to be owner occupied and may not be utilized as 
short term rentals and can help aging residents stay in their homes, or enable young 
families to buy a home, and  
       
      WHEREAS, the Long Island Housing Partnership (LIHP) is willing to act as the 
required partner with the Town of Riverhead to administer the ADU Plus One program, 
should the Town be fortunate enough to receive the funding.  
 
      RESOLVED, That the Town Board hereby authorizes the LIHP to coordinate with 
the Community Development Department to apply for 2M in ADU Plus One funds, and  
       
      NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Community Development 
Department and the LIHP are authorized to negotiate a contract for the administrative 
partnership for the program, subject to Town Board approval. 
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
      SECONDER:    Robert Kern, Councilman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

                                AGREEMENT 

      BETWEEN the TOWN OF RIVERHEAD, a municipal corporation with offices at 4 
West Second Street, Riverhead, New York, hereinafter referred to as ‘TOWN’ and DAVID 
LESSARD, a partnership/corporation/limited liability partnership, with offices at P O Box 139, 
Jamesport, New York, hereinafter referred to as “CONTRACTOR” 

W I T N E S S E T H 

      WHEREAS, the TOWN, in connection with its municipal operations, requires services 
consisting of the following: Seed Clam Administrator – Year 2025; and 

      WHEREAS, the CONTRACTOR is willing to provide the following services to the 
Town: 

      Description of Services:      Administration of Seed Clam Program 

      Date(s) and Hour(s) of Services: Year 2025 

      IT IS HEREBY AGREED by the TOWN and CONTRACTOR as follows: 

   1. That CONTRACTOR shall provide and fully perform, to the TOWN’S satisfaction, the 
      aforementioned services to the TOWN on the date(s) and time(s) stated above. 
       
   2. In return for CONTRACTOR’S services, the TOWN shall pay CONTRACTOR as 
      follows:  The sum of Eight Thousand ($8,000.00) Dollars payable in half-payments of 
      Four Thousand ($4,000.00) Dollars each in April, 2025 and September, 2025. 
       
   3. Administration shall include the bidding process and oversight of facilities to provide 
      seed. The TOWN is responsible for the cost of repair and materials of their rafts, which 
      contain the clams. 

DATED:      Riverhead, New York 


            January _____, 2025 


                                    TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 


 


                                    BY: ___________________________  


                                          TIMOTHY C HUBBARD 


                                          Town Supervisor 


 


                                    CONTRACTOR 


 


                                    BY: ___________________________ 


                                          DAVID LESSARD

                            TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                        
                            TB Resolution 2025-76 
                                        
    AUTHORIZES THE SUPERVISOR TO EXECUTE A 2025 MUSICAL WORKS 
                     LICENSE AGREEMENT WITH SESAC 
                                        
               Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
                  which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
      WHEREAS,   the  Town  of  Riverhead  plays  pre-recorded  music  in  the  form  of 
compact discs, digital video discs, cassettes, and other media in Town facilities and at 
Town events (e.g. the senior center, teen activities); and 
 
      WHEREAS, many of these musical works are protected by U.S. Copyright Law; 
and 
 
      WHEREAS,  a  municipality  requires  permission  from  the  holders  of  such 
copyrights to use the musical works in a public forum; and 
 
      WHEREAS, SESAC LLC represents the holders of copyrights for many of such 
musical works; and 
 
      WHEREAS, SESAC LLC will provide a license granting permission to the Town 
of Riverhead to play all of the works of copyright holders SESAC LLC represents for a 
fee of $1,217.00 for calendar year 2025. 
 
      NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Supervisor is hereby authorized 
to execute the attached license agreement with SESAC LLC for the right to play pre-
recorded music represented by SESAC LLC; and be it further, 
 
      RESOLVED,  that  the  Town  Clerk  is  hereby  directed  to  forward  a  copy  of  this 
resolution  to  the  Accounting  Department;  Parks  and  Recreation;  Senior  Citizen’s 
Services and the Office of the Town Attorney; and be it further,  
 
      RESOLVED,  that  all  Town  Hall  Departments  may  review and  obtain  a  copy  of 
this  resolution  from  the  electronic  storage  device  and, if  needed,  a  certified  copy  of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.   
 
                                  THE VOTE 
                                        
      RESULT:      ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
      MOVER:       Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
      SECONDER:    Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
      AYES:        Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

                        SESAC MUSIC PERFORMANCE LICENSE 
                                   FOR MUNICIPALITIES 

This License Agreement, including any attached and referenced Schedules (the “Agreement”), is made in 
New York by and between SESAC LLC (“SESAC”), a Delaware limited liability company, with offices at 
35 Music Square East, Nashville, TN 37203, and 

                                     LICENSEE Information 

                                                                                                                                             (“LICENSEE”)
                (Municipality Name)                                                                                                                               


                                       Billing Information

                (Street Address)                                                           (City)                                                     (State)                     (Zip)                           

                (Telephone #)                                                             (Fax #)                                                                 (Email)                                                                                        

Those locations within the municipality for which the above supplied information applies (the 
“Municipality”) which are owned, operated or leased by LICENSEE and used as governmental offices or 
which are otherwise under LICENSEE’s sole control; and other locations within the Municipality while 
events under LICENSEE’s sole control are occurring at such locations, are referred to herein as the 
“Premises.” 

SESAC and LICENSEE hereby mutually agree as follows: 

                                     1.  GRANT OF RIGHTS  

Effective as of ______________ 1, 20______ (the “Effective Date”), and subject to the terms and 
conditions of this Agreement, SESAC grants to LICENSEE the non-exclusive right and license to publicly 
perform non-dramatic renditions of all of the musical compositions for which SESAC is authorized to 
license the public performance right (the “Compositions”) solely: (i) on the Premises and/or (ii) via a 
music-on-hold system operated by LICENSEE in connection with the Municipality.   
                                                                                                            Attachment:  Town of Riverhead 2025 Renewal License SESAC (2025-76 : Authorizes the Supervisor to Execute a Musical Works

                                                                                            Packet Pg. 210                                                                                                    9.76.a


                                  2.  LIMITATIONS OF RIGHTS 

A.  Except as specifically described in Paragraph 1, above, nothing contained herein shall be construed 
as permitting LICENSEE to publicly perform, transmit, re-transmit or reproduce any Composition by any 
means, medium, method, device or process now or hereafter known, or as permitting LICENSEE to grant 
any such right to others. 

B.  The rights granted pursuant to Paragraph 1, above, shall exclude “Grand Rights” in and to the 
Compositions (“Grand Rights” include, but are not limited to, the right to perform, in whole or in part, 
dramatico-musical and dramatic works in a dramatic setting). 

C.  The rights granted pursuant to Paragraph 1, above, shall exclude performances of the Compositions: 
(i) which are part of a background music service originating from any location, including the Premises, 
which performances are authorized by SESAC pursuant to a separate license agreement, regardless of 
the means by which such performances are transmitted on or to the Premises, and/or (ii) by coin-
operated phonorecord players (“jukeboxes”), as defined in 17 U.S.C. § 116. 

D.  The authorization provided in this Agreement shall be limited to public performances made in the 
United States of America, its territories, possessions and the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico.  

E.  The rights granted pursuant to Paragraph 1, above, shall exclude performances of the Compositions 
made as part of Sporting Events (“Sporting Events” are professional, semi-professional, major or minor 
league athletic competitions). 

F.  The rights granted pursuant to Paragraph 1, above, shall exclude performances of the Compositions 
made as part of Concerts, other than those promoted solely by LICENSEE (“Concerts” are those 
performances by an entertainer or entertainment group where the primary focus is the performance of 
music).  

G.  The rights granted pursuant to Paragraph 1, above, shall exclude performances of the Compositions 
made by and/or on the premises of colleges and/or universities. 

H.  The rights granted pursuant to Paragraph 1 exclude the right to publicly perform the Compositions 
during political campaign events and/or events organized by political organizations. 

                                        3.  LICENSE FEE 

A.  In consideration of the rights granted herein, LICENSEE shall pay to SESAC an annual license fee 
(each, a “License Fee”) for each calendar year during the Term (each, a “License Fee Period”) in 
accordance with Schedule “A,” which is attached hereto and incorporated herein.   

B.  Notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in this Agreement, SESAC shall have the right, 
upon notice to LICENSEE, to make changes to Schedule “A.”  In such event, LICENSEE shall have the 
right to terminate this Agreement as of the date such change(s) are to take effect, provided that 
LICENSEE gives notice to SESAC of such termination specifically referencing this Paragraph, not later 
than thirty (30) days after SESAC notifies LICENSEE of such change(s).  For the avoidance of doubt, 
annual rate adjustments made pursuant to Paragraph 3.E below shall not be considered a change to 
Schedule “A.”  

C.  Notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in this Agreement, SESAC shall have the right, 
but not the obligation, to verify through independent sources any information required to be reported by 
LICENSEE pursuant to Schedule “A,” and SESAC may adjust the License Fee(s) as may be appropriate 
based on information obtained from such sources. 
                                                                                                            Attachment:  Town of Riverhead 2025 Renewal License SESAC (2025-76 : Authorizes the Supervisor to Execute a Musical Works

                                                                                            Packet Pg. 211                                                                                                    9.76.a


D.  In the event SESAC is determined by any taxing authority or court to be liable for the payment of a 
gross receipts, sales, use, business use or other tax which is based on the amount of SESAC's receipts 
from LICENSEE, then LICENSEE shall reimburse SESAC, within thirty (30) days of notification to 
LICENSEE therefor, for any such tax derived from receipts received from LICENSEE.  

E.  Effective each January 1 following the Effective Date, the rates set forth in the Fee Schedule shall be 
increased by an amount equal to the percent increase in the Consumer Price Index – All Urban 
Consumers (CPI-U) as published by the Bureau of Labor Statistics, U.S. Department of Labor, between 
the most recent October and the preceding October or five percent (5%), whichever amount is greater.    

                       4.  BREACH AND CURE; LATE PAYMENT CHARGE 

A.  In the event LICENSEE is in default or breach of any provision of this Agreement, including failure to 
make any payment when due hereunder, and LICENSEE has not cured such default or breach within 
thirty (30) days following SESAC's notice to LICENSEE thereof, then SESAC shall have the right to 
terminate this Agreement in addition to pursuing any and all other rights and/or remedies.   

B.  Intentionally Omitted.      

                                   5.  INTENTIONALLY OMITTED 

                                     6.  TERM OF LICENSE 

A.  The term of this Agreement shall be for an initial period that commences on the Effective Date and 
continues for a period of twelve (12) calendar months.  

B.  Notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained herein, SESAC shall have the right to terminate 
this Agreement: (i) at any time upon notice to LICENSEE in the event LICENSEE is adjudicated bankrupt, 
or a petition in bankruptcy is filed with respect to LICENSEE, or LICENSEE is declared or becomes 
insolvent; or (ii) upon thirty (30) days’ notice to LICENSEE by reason of any law, rule, decree or other 
enactment having the force of law, by any authority, whether federal, state, local, territorial or otherwise, 
which results in substantial interference in SESAC's operation or a substantial increase in the cost of 
conducting its business.   

                                     7.  MISCELLANEOUS 

A.  This Agreement shall be governed by and subject to the laws of the State of New York, applicable to 
agreements made and to be wholly performed in New York.  This Agreement supersedes and cancels all 
prior negotiations and understandings between SESAC and LICENSEE in connection with the subject 
matter hereof.  If any part of this Agreement is determined invalid or unenforceable by a court of 
competent jurisdiction or by any other legally constituted body having the jurisdiction to make such 
determination, the remainder of this Agreement shall remain in full force and effect.  No waiver of any 
breach of this Agreement shall be deemed a waiver of any preceding, continuing or succeeding breach of 
the same, or any other provision of this Agreement.   

B.  SESAC shall have the right, upon notice to LICENSEE, to withdraw from the scope of this Agreement 
the right to publicly perform any Composition (or collection of Compositions) as to which any action has 
been threatened, instituted or a claim made that SESAC does not have the right to license the 
performance rights in such Composition (or collection of Compositions).     

C.  This Agreement shall not be assignable by LICENSEE without SESAC’s prior written permission.  
Subject to the preceding sentence, this Agreement shall be binding upon and inure to the benefit of 
SESAC’s and LICENSEE’s successors and assigns, but no assignment shall relieve SESAC or 
LICENSEE of its respective obligations under this Agreement.  LICENSEE shall notify SESAC within thirty 
(30) days of any change of ownership or control of LICENSEE’s operations.

executed with the same formality as this Agreement.

                     100,001 - 150,000                    $ 2,886

                     250,001 - 500,000                    $ 5,162 
                     500,001 And over          $6,533 + $610 for each additional 
                                                     100,000 population 
 
2.  LICENSE FEE PAYMENT. 
 
Upon the execution of this Agreement, LICENSEE shall pay the initial License Fee to SESAC which 
amount shall be prorated (if applicable) to reflect payment for the period from the Effective Date through 
the end of such License Fee Period.  The License Fee for each License Fee Period thereafter shall be 
submitted to SESAC on or before the commencement of such License Fee Period. 
 
3.  REPORTING. 
 
A.  Upon the execution of this Agreement, LICENSEE shall submit to SESAC a completed license fee 
report in the form attached hereto as Schedule “B” (each, a “License Fee Report”), which is incorporated 
herein.  Said initial License Fee Report shall set forth the Population of the Municipality as of the Effective 
Date. 
 
B.  On or before each October 1 during the Term following the Effective Date, LICENSEE shall provide 
SESAC with an updated License Fee Report setting forth the Population of the Municipality as of the 
preceding September 1; provided, however, LICENSEE shall not be required to submit any License Fee 
Report which would contain the same Population as the most recently submitted License Fee Report. 
 
C.  All reports under this Agreement shall be submitted by LICENSEE, by electronic means if possible, in 
Excel or similar format if applicable, to reporting@sesac.com, or by regular mail addressed to: 
 
       SESAC 
       35 Music Square East  
       Nashville, TN 37203 
 
4.  DEFINITIONS. 
 
“Population” means the total population of the municipality as of the most recent United States Census.

or which will be, provided by LICENSEE pursuant to this Schedule “A” to be complete, true and accurate.

  AUTHORIZES THE SUPERVISOR TO EXECUTE A STIPULATION WITH LOCAL 
   1000, AFSCME, AFL-CIO, RIVERHEAD UNIT OF THE SUFFOLK LOCAL #852 
                                        
               Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
                    which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
      WHEREAS, the Chief of Police has requested a promotion for a CSEA Union 
employee in a title that is not currently used by the Town of Riverhead, Public Safety 
Dispatcher III; and 
       
      WHEREAS, the CSEA Public Safety Dispatcher (PSD) salary schedule has 
group 1 for the title Public Safety Dispatcher I and group 2 for the title Public Safety 
Dispatcher II; and 
 
      WHEREAS, to accompany this title, the Town of Riverhead proposed to the 
CSEA that a new group, to be known as group 3, be added to the Public Safety 
Dispatcher (PSD) salary schedule for 2025 and forward to accommodate this new title, 
and the CSEA has subsequently agreed;  
 
      NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board be and hereby 
approves the stipulation outlined in this resolution and authorizes the Supervisor to 
execute same; and be it further 
 
      RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby directed to forward a copy of 
this resolution to Town Attorney, CSEA Unit President Terri DeFilippis, the Financial 
Administrator and the Personnel Officer. Town Hall Departments may review and obtain 
a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage device, and if needed, a certified 
copy of same can be obtained from the office of the Town Clerk.

                          LICENSE AGREEMENT 
                             BETWEEN THE 
                          TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                  AND 
                   THE RESEARCH FOUNDATION FOR  
                 THE STATE UNIVERSITY OF NEW YORK  
                                      
      This Contract is made and entered into as of this ______ day of January , 
2025, by and between the Town of Riverhead located at 4 West Second Street, 
Riverhead, County of Suffolk and State of New York (“Town”) and the Research 
Foundation for the State University of New York, is a private, nonprofit corporation 
on behalf of the State University of New York (“SUNY”) having a principal place of 
business at 35 State Street, Albany, NY 12207-2826 (“RFSUNY”). 
      WHEREAS, RFSUNY is a private, non-profit, education corporation whose 
primary responsibility is to administer grants and sponsored programs on behalf of 
the  SUNY  and  facilitates  research, education,  and  public  service  at  30  state-
operated SUNY campuses, including Stony Brook University (“SBU”); 
      WHEREAS, RFSUNY, through its researchers at SBU, and the Town, among 
other things, have a mutual interest in protecting Long Island’s shorelines, waters, 
and marine life;   
      WHEREAS,  the  Town  owns  fee  title  to  land  in  Riverhead,  New  York, 
commonly known as Grangebel Park (the “Park”), which land is depicted in Exhibit 
A attached hereto and made a part hereof; and  
      WHEREAS, the RFSUNY desires a license agreement for RFSUNY to enter 
and use a portion of the Park for the installation and continued monitoring of video 
camera within an enclosure box, measuring 48 inches long x 39 inches wide x 32 
inches in height to be placed in the waters at the Park fishway, which RFSUNY will 
use the video camera to determine the number of alewives entering the fishway and 
passing upstream to spawn during the months of March, April and May of 2023 and 
further, RFSUNY will require and seeks permission to use the electric current at the 
Park to power the video camera; and .  
                                                                                    Attachment:  SUNY Research Grangebel Fish Passage LICENSE AGREEMENT 2025 (2025-78 : Authorizes Execution of a License Agreement


                                                                        Packet Pg. 220                                                                              9.78.a


      WHEREAS, the Town desires to grant to RFSUNY a license to enter and use 
a portion of the Park designated herein as the Licensed Area, and permission to use 
the electric current at the Park for the purposes set forth above commencing on 
February  1,  2025 and  ending  on  June  15,  2025,  unless  terminated  earlier  as 
provided herein.  
      NOW THEREFORE, in consideration of the mutual covenants hereinafter set 
forth, the parties agree as follows: 
      1.    Licensed  Area,  Use  and  Term:  The  area  licensed  by  Research 
Foundation for the State University of New York hereunder (the “Licensed Area”) 
shall consist of that portion or portions of the waterway in the Park as depicted by 
the cross-hatching on Exhibit A attached hereto and made a part hereof and shall 
include the improvements thereon including but not limited to any building, structure, 
any  necessary  equipment  and  any  appurtenances  thereto,  such  as  appropriate 
means for ingress and egress upon the terms and conditions set forth hereunder.  
This  License  will  provide  RFSUNY  and  its  employees,  representatives,  agents, 
including the same from SUNY, use and occupancy of the Property commencing on 
execution of this agreement and ending on June 15, 2025 (the "Term") for purposes 
of installation and continued monitoring of the enclosure box and video camera to 
record the alewives spawning movements upstream, together with permission to 
use the electric current (collectively, the "Permitted Use").   Either party may cancel 
the agreement without cause at any time upon fifteen (15) days written notice. 
      2.    Compliance With Laws:  RFSUNY shall at all times during the Term, 
comply with  all  applicable  federal,  state,  county and municipal laws,  regulations, 
ordinances,  codes  and  restrictions,  including,  without  limitation,  compliance  with 
Article 28 of the New York State Tax Law and applicable regulations thereunder 
arising  out  of  Licensee's  Permitted  Use  and  will  secure  any  and  all  permits  or 
licenses required for its activities and operations carried out at the Licensed Area.  
Town agrees to cooperate with RFSUNY by providing any information at its disposal 

                                    2 
                                                                                    Attachment:  SUNY Research Grangebel Fish Passage LICENSE AGREEMENT 2025 (2025-78 : Authorizes Execution of a License Agreement


                                                                        Packet Pg. 221                                                                              9.78.a


and otherwise use its best efforts to assist RFSUNY in pursuing its applications for 
all necessary approvals. 
      3.    Compensation:   It  is  agreed  by  and  between  the  parties  that  no 
compensation or fee shall be required for the License set forth above.     
      4.    Responsibilities of Licensee:   At the conclusion of the license period, 
RFSUNY will promptly commence garbage and rubbish removal and cleanup (the 
“Cleanup”) so that the Property is delivered back to the Town in the same condition 
(normal wear and tear excepted) as delivered to RFSUNY on the commencement 
date of the Term.  RFSUNY will remove the enclosure, video camera and electric 
powers cords and any refuse, rubble, garbage and debris created as a result of its 
use and activities at the Property and dispose of the same at an appropriate waste 
facility. 
      5.         Authority of Town:   Town  represents  and  warrants  that  it  owns  fee 
title to the Licensed Area and has all the requisite authority necessary to enter into 
this agreement. 
      6.    Insurance  and  Indemnification:  RFSUNY  will  be  responsible  for 
providing comprehensive general liability insurance in the amount of not less than 
$1,000,000.00 with a company or companies reasonably satisfactory to Town. (In 
addition,  RFSUNY  will  provide  casualty  insurance  on  the  buildings,  structures, 
equipment and facilities within the Property at their full replacement cost.)  RFSUNY 
shall provide certificates of the foregoing insurance, showing the Town of Riverhead 
as additional insureds to the extent of their interest.  RFSUNY agrees to indemnify 
and  hold  harmless  Town  of  Riverhead  and  their  respective  officers,  employees, 
agents, representatives and officials from any and all loss or liability arising out of 
Licensee's use of the Property as described herein including liability for damages to 
property or for injuries or death to persons which may arise from, or be attributable 
or incident to the use by RFSUNY and its employees, agents, representatives and 
concessionaires,  or any concert attendee, of the Property, excepting liability solely

caused by the negligence of the Town of Riverhead or their respective employees, 
agents or representatives.  
      7.    Miscellaneous  Responsibilities  of Licensee:  Except  with  respect  to 
any specific services, equipment and facilities to be provided by Town under this 
Agreement, RFSUNY will be responsible for acquiring all services and materials and 
otherwise for carrying out all actions necessary in connection with the project and 
related activities to take place, including, but not limited to, all planning, operations, 
concessions, garbage removal, cleanup, construction and demolition or removal of 
all temporary structures, development.  RFSUNY will obtain all necessary approvals 
required for the Project and for construction of any temporary structure or system to 
be used at the Licensed Area in connection with the Project or related activities.  
Town  shall  use  its  best  efforts  to  facilitate  the  Licensee’s  acquisition  of  such 
necessary approvals.  In addition, RFSUNY will take all actions necessary to restore 
the Property to its condition existing on the date of the commencement of the Term 
(normal wear and tear excepted) under this agreement, including, without limiting 
the generality of the foregoing, the removal of all temporary structures and systems. 
      8.    Successors and Assigns.  This agreement shall be binding upon and 
inure  to  the  benefit  of  the  respective  successors  and  assigns  of  the  parties; 
provided, however, that nothing herein shall be deemed to permit the assignment of 
this Agreement by either party without the express written consent of the other party.  
RFSUNY  shall,  however  be  allowed  to  change  the  name  of  either  the  RFSUNY 
entity  or the  name  of the  Project  in  its  sole discretion  without  requiring  the prior 
consent of Town thereto.  Additionally in the event Town conveys the Park or any 
part thereof during the period of time from the date hereof to the end of the Term 
(and/or any Option Term) any successor in interest to Town shall be bound to the 
obligations and responsibilities of Town herein and Licensee’s use and occupancy 
rights herein shall not be disturbed by any successor in-interest to Town.

rights and obligations of both the Town and RFSUNY hereunder are conditioned on
